   454 0000029E [D3130000]          <1>         dd	_qpop
   455 000002A2 [E6130000]          <1>         dd	_qpush
   456 000002A6 [93140000]          <1>         dd	_ex
   457 000002AA [0D140000]          <1>         dd	_dpush
   458 000002AE [7B1B0000]          <1>         dd	_lsc

   464 000002C2 [86140000]          <1>         dd	_dl

   466 000002CA [D21A0000]          <1>         dd	_dan
   467 000002CE [8C1B0000]          <1>         dd	_dlsc
   468 000002D2 [92140000]          <1>         dd	_spare

   471                              <1> 
   472                                  	%include	"rw.msm"
   473                              <1> 
   474                              <1> 
   475                              <1> ;	include	rta_x86.h
   476                              <1> ;	.model	large
   477                              <1> ;	.code
   478                              <1> 
   479                              <1> ;	this is the operand reader / writer
   480                              <1> ;	for emulated RTA1 on x86
   481                              <1> 
   482                              <1> ;	layout is
   483                              <1> 
   484                              <1> ;	RTA1 24-bit registers are modeled in an array of
   485                              <1> ;	platform-endian integers. In x86 these are 32-bit
   486                              <1> ;	little-endian integers
   487                              <1> 
   488                              <1> ;	platform-endian doesn't affect registers
   489                              <1> ;	because endianness is not at the CPU
   490                              <1> ;	side of the bus, but at the memory side
   491                              <1> 
   492                              <1> ;	when Intel circuitry in the x86 CPU staticises the value
   493                              <1> ;	of an emulated register, that value is big endian
   494                              <1> 
   495                              <1> ;	the stored integers where emulated registers are modeled
   496                              <1> ;	are platform-endian, with identical effect on big and
   497                              <1> ;	little endian emulator platforms
   498                              <1> 
   499                              <1> ;	RTA1 24-bit executable space storage words are modeled in
   500                              <1> ;	another array of platform-endian 32-bit integers. Emulation
   501                              <1> ;	on x86 swaps the byte order of storage words on read and
   502                              <1> ;	before write to conform with RTA1 canonical storage order
   503                              <1> 
   504                              <1> ;       RTA1 architecture has registers in the first 256 locations
   505                              <1> ;       of address space and access differentiates registers from
   506                              <1> ;       from memory according to effective address
   507                              <1> 
   508                              <1> ;	location of registers and storage are handed to read / write
   509                              <1> ;	routines as RTA1 word linear effective addresses
   510                              <1> 
   511                              <1> ;	These routines maintain the RTA1 linear addresses passed
   512                              <1> ;	in x86 registers and apply them with shifted scale plus
   513                              <1> ;	displacement, for example
   514                              <1> 
   515                              <1> ;		mov	eax, dword ptr [edi+esi*4+_memory]
   516                              <1> ;		bswap	eax
   517                              <1> ;		mov	dword_ptr [ebp+ebx*4], eax
   518                              <1> 
   519                              <1> ;	RTA1 register addresses are already absolute in terms of
   520                              <1> ;	the emulated RTA1 machine
   521                              <1> 
   522                              <1> ;	ebp points at the context register frame. There are two
   523                              <1> ;	register frames, application and interrupt. Registers
   524                              <1> ;	addressed as storage operand are in a single list
   525                              <1> 
   526                              <1> ;		mov	eax, dword ptr [esi*4+__register]
   527                              <1> 
   528                              <1> ;	RTA1 storage addresses are translated by RTA1 relocation
   529                              <1> ;	architecture before application. The updated linear addresses
   530                              <1> ;	of the emulated machine are in esi
   531                              <1> 
   532                              <1> ;	The operand routines in this file point edi to the x86 platform
   533                              <1> ;	storage array start of the storage device, most often emulated
   534                              <1> ;	RTA1 executable space
   535                              <1> 
   536                              <1> ;	instructions call these operand routines with RTA1 effective 
   537                              <1> ;	address in eax
   538                              <1> 
   539                              <1> ;	instructions receive load operand values in eax and ebx, or in
   540                              <1> ;	a list of RTA1 emulated register locations pointed by ebp+ebx
   541                              <1> 
   542                              <1> ;	store instructions submit a value in ebx, or values in list of
   543                              <1> ;	RTA1 emulated register locations pointed by ebp+ebx
   544                              <1> 
   545                              <1> ;	to preserve linear address consistency, application instruction
   546                              <1> ;	work areas, where needed in addition to x86 registers, are
   547                              <1> ;	implemented as sub-architectural extra RTA1 registers at the end
   548                              <1> ;	of the 256-longword register stack. x86 register ebp+ebx*4 identify
   549                              <1> ;	these locations by linear RTA1 word quantum as "registers"
   550                              <1> 
   551                              <1> ;	RTA1 registers and storage alike are in 24-bit word address quantum space
   552                              <1> 
   553                              <1> ;	emulated instructions loading or storing multiple hidden extra work
   554                              <1> ;	registers should unconditionally set ebp to the start or application
   555                              <1> ;	frame of the emulated register array, so that [ebp+ebx*4] accesses the
   556                              <1> ;	correct locations at register occurence 256+
   557                              <1> 
   558                              <1> ;               _floating_operand2 equ  256+12
   559                              <1> 
   560                              <1> ;		push	ebp
   561                              <1> ;		mov	ebp, __register	; point to application register frame[0]
   562                              <1> ;		mov	ebx, 256+_floating_operand2
   563                              <1> ;		call	_burst_read4
   564                              <1> 
   565                              <1> ;		pop	ebp		; return to previous register frame[0] application
   566                              <1> 					;                          or frame[1] interrupt
   567                              <1> 
   568                              <1> ;	Both internal stack pointers are also absolute, so for stack operations
   569                              <1> ;	ebp should be momentarily forced to the lower-addressed (application) stack
   570                              <1> ;	frame after being used to point the stack location of reference
   571                              <1> 
   572                              <1> ;		mov	ebx, dword ptr [ebp+S_P]	; read one of the two stack pointers
   573                              <1> ;		cmp	ebx, ebp+STACK_LOWER_LIMIT	; 24*4 within context of either stack
   574                              <1> ;		jl	II_GUARD
   575                              <1> ;		add	ebx, -1				; new stack top
   576                              <1> ;		mov	dword ptr [ebp+S_P], ebx
   577                              <1> ;		push	ebp				; which ever stack pointer it is, it points
   578                              <1> ;		mov	ebp,__register			; relative to all the register stack
   579                              <1> ;		call	_operand_read			; for I am the single-word push instruction
   580                              <1> ;		pop	ebp				;
   581                              <1> 
   582                              <1> ;	register identities supplied from emulated instructions to these routines
   583                              <1> ;	are their lowercase names equated to RTA1 word addresses
   584                              <1> 
   585                              <1> ;	There exist also uppercase spellings which instruction routines may
   586                              <1> ;	access internally. The uppercase names are four times in value the
   587                              <1> ;	equivalent lowercase ordinal names to give x86 platform offset values
   588                              <1> 
   589                              <1> ;       Assembly language equate is like parentheses! What's in a label
   590                              <1> ;       is not an expression but its value. Nothing like C preprocessor.
   591                              <1> ;       Just in case you're developing enhancements in assembly using
   592                              <1> ;       preprocessor and #define
   593                              <1> 
   594                              <1> ;		_floating_operand2 equ	256+12
   595                              <1> ;		FLOATING_OPERAND2 equ	_floating_operand2*4
   596                              <1> 
   597                              <1> 
   598                              <1> ;		a	equ	4
   599                              <1> ;		b	equ	5
   600                              <1> ;		mantissa2 equ	6
   601                              <1> 
   602                              <1> ;		A	equ	a*4
   603                              <1> ;		B	equ	b*4
   604                              <1> ;		MANTISSA2 equ	mantissa2*4
   605                              <1> 
   606                              <1> ;		mov	ebx, dword ptr [bp+MANTISSA2]	; the very same!
   607                              <1> ;		mov	ebx, dword ptr [bp+mantissa2*4]	; the very same
   608                              <1> 
   609                              <1> ;	but to identify an instruction-implied register to these operand routines
   610                              <1> 
   611                              <1> ;		mov	ebx, mantissa2		; bp already says which register set
   612                              <1> 
   613                              <1> ;	instruction evaluation supplies right-hand side operand EA in eax
   614                              <1> ;	Instruction implementation needs not examine EA. Call _operand_read
   615                              <1> ;	or _operand_write. eax must be as supplied to the instruction routine
   616                              <1> ;	on on operand retrieve and store
   617                              <1> 
   618                              <1> ;	simple instructions receive operand mode in cl from instruction
   619                              <1> ;	evaluation
   620                              <1> 
   621                              <1> ;	shifts and jumps use the ea which is already indexed or indirected
   622                              <1> ;	if necessary and make no operand call
   623                              <1> 
   624                              <1> ;	instructions call _burst_read2 or _burst_write2 for two-word operand cycles
   625                              <1> ;	instructions call _burst_read4 or _burst_write4 for four-word operand cycles
   626                              <1> 
   627                              <1> ;	operand reads of 1 or 2 words return values in eax:ebx
   628                              <1> 
   629                              <1> ;		call	_burst_read2
   630                              <1> ;		mov	dword ptr [ebp+A], eax
   631                              <1> ;		mov	dword ptr [ebp+B], ebx
   632                              <1> 
   633                              <1> ;	to store one operand word place it in ebx
   634                              <1> 
   635                              <1> ;	_sc	mov	ebx, dword ptr[_psr]	; I am the store carry instruction sc
   636                              <1> ;		and	ebx, 1			; CARRY
   637                              <1> ;		call	_operand_write
   638                              <1> 
   639                              <1> ;	to store two or four words or to load four words, point bx to register
   640                              <1> 
   641                              <1> ;	_qpop	mov	ebx, dword ptr [ebp+S_P] ; internal stack pointer
   642                              <1> ;						; either application sp or interrupt sp
   643                              <1> ;
   644                              <1> ;		add	dword ptr [ebp+S_P], 4	; internal stack+= 4
   645                              <1> ;		push	ebp			;
   646                              <1> ;		mov	ebp, __register		; in case context is interrupt registers
   647                              <1> ;		call	_burst_write4		; both internal stack pointers are absolute
   648                              <1> ;		pop	ebp			; point epb back to application registers
   649                              <1> ;						;                or interrupt registers
   650                              <1> 
   651                              <1> ;	more complex instructions do something to the registers after
   652                              <1> ;	acquiring operands
   653                              <1> 
   654                              <1> ;		call	_operand_read
   655                              <1> ;		add	eax, dword ptr [ebp+A]
   656                              <1> ;		rol	eax
   657                              <1> ;		and	al, CARRY		; 1
   658                              <1> ;		or	byte ptr [_psr], al	; low-order byte of longword _psr
   659                              <1> ;		shr	eax, 8
   660                              <1> ;		mov	dword ptr [ebp+A], eax
   661                              <1> 
   662                              <1> ;	emulated RTA1 instructions which both read and write (modify)
   663                              <1> ;	storage use the address in [edi+esi*4] to rewrite. edi is
   664                              <1> ;	NULL if it's not a suitable memory for a modify operation
   665                              <1> 
   666                              <1> ;	modify instructions which may have a register operand (not TS)
   667                              <1> ;	call _operand_write to rewrite a register. This guards aganst
   668                              <1> ;	applications writing interrupt registers.
   669                              <1>  
   670                              <1> ;	the effect of storage buses characteristically different
   671                              <1> ;	from RTA1 executable space is emulated in the routines
   672                              <1> ;	device_read and device_write
   673                              <1> 
   674                              <1> ;	Peripheral bus types implemented are
   675                              <1> 
   676                              <1> ;		filestore containing extents of up to 768K octets
   677                              <1> ;		accessible to RTA1 as up to 256K words in each extent.
   678                              <1> ;		The 3-octet words are in canonical order and packed
   679                              <1> 
   680                              <1> ;		network interface buffer store shared with the emulator
   681                              <1> ;		platform and reading out to RTA1 at 16 data bits per word
   682                              <1> ;		with eight high-order zero bits. RTA writes 16 data bits
   683                              <1> ;		to these locations from register low-order bit positions.
   684                              <1> ;		Storage byte order is canonical. These buffers are normal
   685                              <1> ;		and contiguous byte arrays of the emulator platform.
   686                              <1> ;		To RTA1 they are an attached device array of 16-bit words
   687                              <1> 
   688                              <1> ;	Device array types are
   689                              <1> 
   690                              <1> ;		executable space
   691                              <1> ;		24-bit filestore array
   692                              <1> ;		16-bit network interface array
   693                              <1> 
   694                              <1> ;	devices are identified in RTA1 memory relocation pointers and
   695                              <1> ;	tagged with device type. Executable space is device zero
   696                              <1>

  1267                              <1> ;	sub-architectural measure on sabr and reload instructions
  1268                              <1> 
  1269                              <1> ;	check the target memory block is in range and the bus characteristic
  1270                              <1> ;	of the memory device when selecting blocks of memory, not when
  1271                              <1> ;	accessing them. Use 8 spare bits in the word containing _base[]
  1272                              <1> ;	for a quick recall of the emulated bus attribute on reference
  1273                              <1> 
  1274                              <1> ;	because this software emulation needs to act differently for
  1275                              <1> 
  1276                              <1> ;		executable space	rta1 24-bit words canonical memory
  1277                              <1> ;					modeled in platform 32-bit words
  1278                              <1> 
  1279                              <1> ;		shared network buffers	16-bit words canonical in memory
  1280                              <1> ;					and zero extend on readout to RTA1
  1281                              <1> 
  1282                              <1> ;		24-bit filestore array	3-octet words stored big-endian
  1283                              <1> ;					in packed array
  1284                              <1> 
  1285                              <1> ;	concept RTA1 device arrays with bus behaviour differences are completely
  1286                              <1> ;	emulated on PC emulations because device arrays are modeled in PC RAM.
  1287                              <1> 
  1288                              <1> ;	Various bus behaviours are emulated transparently to RTA1 target software
  1289                              <1> ;	in anticipation	that different memories for different uses may be attached
  1290                              <1> ;	on product boards, making core-emulated RTA1s much more efficient for not
  1291                              <1> ;	needing this part of emulation
  1292                              <1> 
  1293                              <1> ;	devices
  1294                              <1> 
  1295                              <1> ;	device 0 is always executable space, but there may be more devices
  1296                              <1> ;	with bus characteristics like device 0. The device descriptors are
  1297                              <1> 
  1298                              <1> ;		_________________________________________________________________
  1299                              <1> ;		| 16 bits flags	| 16 bits banks	|       32 bits pointer		|
  1300                              <1> ;		|_______________|____high index_|_______________________________|
  1301                              <1> 
  1302                              <1> 
  1303                              <1> ;	[out]	sabr	[go]	[call]	reload instructions call here
  1304                              <1> ;	go and call can probably check quicker themself
  1305                              <1> ;	out can be trusted because applications don't out memory _base[] ports
  1306                              <1> 
  1307                              <1> ;	a big block in an RTA1 address window is 262144 words.
  1308                              <1> ;	this checking concerns address windows tagged 2..63
  1309                              <1> ;	a device is an array up to 65536 big blocks or banks
  1310                              <1> 
  1311                              <1> ;	you get here with the relocation handle in ebx
  1312                              <1> ;	and the target window tag in eax, because that is the EA of a sabr instruction
  1313                              <1> 
  1314                              <1> device_read:				; readout device arrays

  2037                                  	%include	"stack.msm"
  2038                              <1> ;	stack operations call these to add or subract stack
  2039                              <1> ;	limits are checked here
  2040                              <1> ;	these routines always leave epb -> all registers 0..255
  2041                              <1> ;	because both  interrupt internal stack pointer register 128 + 15
  2042                              <1> ;		and application internal stack pointer register 15
  2043                              <1> 
  2044                              <1> ;	are absolute pointers to the entire register stack
  2045                              <1> 
  2046                              <1> ;	therefore instructions calling here must afterwards
  2047                              <1> 
  2048                              <1> ;		mov	ebp, dword ptr [_register_set]
  2049                              <1> 
  2050                              <1> ;	to get ebp back to application registers 0..127
  2051                              <1> ;			or interrupt registers 128..255
  2052                              <1> 
  2053                              <1> ;	ebp governs which r k x y a b mantissa2 mantissa3 fp sp is implied in the instruction opcode
  2054                              <1> ;	registers addressed as operand are always absolute in the range 0..255
  2055                              <1> 
  2056                              <1> ;	these don't move any data but leave [ebp+ebx*4] pointing to the required stack frame
  2057                              <1> ;	and update the stack pointer
  2058                              <1> 
  2059                              <1> ;	although applications can and must read interrupt registers with load instructions
  2060                              <1> ;	they can't read interrupt registers with runaway pop instructions
  2061                              <1> ;	because the problem is easier to find with an interrupt as soon as 128+ gets popped
  2062                              <1> 
  2063                              <1>

  2780                              <1> 	%if	1
  2781                              <1> 
  2782                              <1> ;	this divide made from 2 Intel divides should be a better method
  2783                              <1> ;	than the procession of 1-bit shifts and test subtracts
  2784                              <1> ;	which is the %else which it replaces. That also works
  2785                              <1> 
  2786                              <1> ;	this converts to and from positive magnitude
  2787                              <1> ;	because zoning the 2nd divide with a zero 1st remainder
  2788                              <1> ;	can't tell +0 from -0 in platform 2s complement
  2789                              <1> 
  2790                              <1> ;	polarity conversions before and after need no explanation
  2791                              <1> 
  2792                              <1> ;	1st dividend is 48 zero bits and high order 16 data bits
  2793                              <1> ;	of the the 48-bit RTA1 dividend
  2794                              <1> 
  2795                              <1> ;	2nd dividend is 1st remainder and the remaining 32 bits
  2796                              <1> ;	the the RTA1 dividend
  2797                              <1> 
  2798                              <1> ;	input is compressed from 24-bit words and output unpacked
  2799                              <1> ;	to 24-bit words
  2800                              <1> 
  2801                              <1> ;	64-bit dividend in 386 mode is high order bits in edx, low in eax
  2802                              <1> ;	platform faults if quotient carries from eax. Remainder in edx
  2803                              <1> 
  2804                              <1> ;	RTA1 quotient is 48 bits so it takes 2 divides in 32-bit mode
  2805                              <1> 
  2806                              <1> _divide:
  2807 0000171F 52                  <1> 	push	edx

  2819 0000173F 7473                <1> 	jz	_d_ont		; zero results in eax ebx already

  2842 0000177A F7F3                <1> 	div	ebx

  2844 0000177D F7F3                <1> 	div	ebx		; generate 2nd quotient

  2847 00001782 7903                <1> 	jns	_d_remainder_plus

  2853 0000178D 87D1                <1> 	xchg	edx, ecx	; remainder -> ecx / final sign -> edx
  2854                              <1>

  2861 00001797 F7D3                <1> 	not	ebx		; invert + increment quotient
  2862 00001799 66F7D0              <1> 	not	ax		; RTA1 integer is also 2s complement
  2863 0000179C 81C301000000        <1> 	add	ebx, 1
  2864 000017A2 66150000            <1> 	adc	ax, 0
